ترجمہ: پھر جب کوئی روایت موجود نہ ہو ہمارے فہم و بصیرت رکھنے والے علماء سے اور بعد کے فقہاء میں اختلاف ہو جائے تو اس قول کو ترجیح دی جائے گی جو اکثر فقہاء مثلاً امام طحاوی، ابو حفص كبير ، ابو جعفر ہندوانی ، اور مشہور ابواللیث سمرقندی جیسے حضرات کا ہو، اور جہاں ان حضرات کا کوئی قول موجود نہ ہو اور فتوی دینے کی ضرورت ہو تو مفتی پوری کوشش اور محنت سے غور و فکر کرے اور چاہئے کہ پرودرگار کی قیامت کے دن کی پکڑ سے ڈرے، اس لئے کہ احکام شرعیہ کو بیان کرنے میں وہی شخص دلیری کرتا ہے جو بد بخت اور مقصد میں نا کام آدمی ہوتا ہے۔ پھر ہم اگر نہ پائیں کوئی روایت ایسی جو صاحب درایت اعلام سے ہو مروی ہو بعد کے مشائخ میں اختلاف پیدا اکثر کے قول پر تب مبنی رہے گا فتوی
Then when no narration is found from our scholars of understanding and the later ones differ, the one which the majority (such as al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far, and al-Layth al-Shahir) agree upon is given weight. And where no opinion is found for these, and there is need for ifta, the mufti should look with utmost seriousness and ijtihad, and fear the punishment of his Lord on the Day of Return, for none dares to speak on the rulings except a wretched, failing person.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents a key rule in Hanafi fatwa methodology for when there is no transmitted opinion from the early authoritative scholars (ashab al-darayah). The hierarchy is: first look for a riwaya from the early Hanafi authorities like Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar. If none, then look for the opinion of the majority of later scholars (mutakhkhirin) such as Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, al-Tahawi, and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. If those also have no recorded opinion, the mufti must exercise his own ijtihad (tahqiq al-manat) with full seriousness and fear of Allah, because issuing fatwa without proper knowledge is dangerous. This rule highlights the Hanafi emphasis on following transmitted authority and the heavy responsibility of ijtihad.

Key Terms
رِوَايَة (riwaya): A transmitted opinion from the early Hanafi scholars (mujtahidun fi al-madhhab).
دِرَايَة (darayah): Deep understanding and insight in fiqh, characterizing the early scholars whose opinions are authoritative.
تَرْجِيح (tarjih): Giving preference to one opinion over others based on strength or majority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule given in this passage, if there is no riwaya from the early authorities (ashab al-darayah) and the later scholars disagree, which opinion should be given preference?
A) The opinion of the mufti's own ijtihad
B) The opinion held by the majority of later scholars such as al-Tahawi and Abu Hafs al-Kabir
C) The opinion of the local judge
D) The opinion of the common people

Key Takeaway
In the absence of riwaya, the mufti must first adopt the majority view of later Hanafi authorities (like al-Tahawi), and only as a last resort engage in ijtihad.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Rules of Preference in Fatwa When No Riwaya Exists
Two rasm al-mufti rules for preferring scholarly opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the two rasm al-mufti rules: the hierarchy of preference when no riwaya is found, and the special rule for ibadat preferring Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion.

Core Idea
When no riwaya exists, follow the majority of later scholars; in ibadat, default to Imam's view unless his own riwaya says otherwise.

A mufti often faces cases where no transmitted ruling (riwaya) from the early Hanafi masters is available. This lesson presents two key rules to guide the mufti in such situations. The first rule establishes a hierarchy among later scholars and outlines when personal ijtihad becomes necessary. The second rule provides a default preference for Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion in matters of worship, with a specific condition that prevents blind adherence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the absence of riwaya
First, confirm that no riwaya from the early Hanafi scholars (like Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) exists for the issue at hand. The rule applies only when riwaya is absent.
Riwaya refers to transmitted rulings from the founding imams, recorded in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah or other rare transmissions.
2
Check opinions of later scholars
If later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) differ, preference is given to the opinion held by the majority among authorities like Imam al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. Identify which position most of these scholars support.
These scholars are among the later authoritative figures. Their consensus or majority view carries weight.
3
Apply the ijtihad fallback
If even these later authorities have no stated opinion, the mufti must exert his own ijtihad with utmost care and fear of Allah. This step requires deep knowledge and caution.
The passage warns that issuing fatwa without proper knowledge is reckless.
4
Apply the special rule for ibadat
For all matters of worship (ibadat), the default rule is to prefer Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion absolutely. However, this is conditional: if there exists an authentic riwaya from Imam Abu Hanifa that others (e.g., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) have adopted a different position, then that riwaya takes precedence.
The example given is tayammum for a person who throws dates into water, illustrating that even in ibadat, a contrary riwaya can override the default.

Then, when no riwaya is found from our scholars of insight, and the later scholars have differed, preference is given to the opinion of the majority, such as at-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far, and al-Layth ash-Shahir. And when no statement of these is found and there is need for fatwa, the mufti should look with utmost effort and ijtihad, and fear the grip of his Lord on the Day of Return, for none dares to issue rulings except a wretched one who fails his objective. ... And here are some verified rules that have been established among the people of understanding: In all chapters of worship, the opinion of Imam (Abu Hanifa) is given preference absolutely, as long as there is not authenticated a riwaya from him that others have taken, such as the case of tayammum for one who has thrown dates into water.

Commentary
This passage presents two important rasm rules for a mufti. The first rule addresses the scenario when no transmission (riwaya) is found from the early Hanafi scholars (the 'asatidha' or our scholars of insight). In that case, if later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) differ, the mufti should give preference to the opinion of the majority, especially those like Imam Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, and Abu al-Layth as-Samarqandi. If even these later authorities have no statement, the mufti must exert personal ijtihad with utmost caution and fear of Allah, as issuing fatwa without knowledge is reckless. The second rule deals specifically with matters of worship (ibadat). In all chapters of ibadat, the default rule is to prefer Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion absolutely, unless there is an authentic riwaya from Imam Abu Hanifa himself that his opponents (e.g., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) have adopted a different view. The example given is tayammum for a person who has put dates into water (the water becomes musta'mal? The specific ruling is not detailed here, but it illustrates that even in ibadat, a contrary riwaya can override the default preference).

Key Terms
رِوَايَة (riwāyah): A transmission of a legal ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa or other early scholars, specifically as recorded in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah or rare transmissions.
إِمَام (Imām): Imam Abu Hanifa (al-Nu'man ibn Thabit).
ضَوَابِط (ḍawābiṭ): Sub-maxims or precise rules that qualify the application of broader qawa'id.

Key Takeaway
When no riwaya exists, a mufti must follow a two-tier hierarchy: for non-ibadat, prefer the majority of later scholars (like Tahawi and Abu Hafs); for ibadat, default to Imam Abu Hanifa's view unless his own riwaya contradicts it.

The Default and Exception in Ibadat: Following Imam Abu Hanifa's Opinion
States a rasm al-mufti rule for tarjih in ibadat with an exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of tarjih in ibadat by identifying when to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's well-known view versus when to follow a riwaya adopted by another imam.

Core Idea
In worship, the mufti defaults to Imam Abu Hanifa — unless a riwaya from him adopted by another imam overrides.

This lesson introduces a key rasm al-mufti rule specific to ibadat: the mufti generally gives precedence to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion. However, a precise exception exists when a transmission from the Imam himself has been taken up by another major Hanafi figure such as Abu Yusuf or Muhammad. Understanding this rule prevents incorrect fatwa giving in matters of worship, ensuring internal school consistency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default preference
State that in all chapters of worship, the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa is given preference absolutely unless a specific condition is met.
The word 'مُطْلَقًا' (absolutely) emphasizes the strength of the default.
2
Identify the overriding condition
The exception occurs when there is a proven riwaya (transmission) from Abu Hanifa that has been adopted by another imam (such as Abu Yusuf or Muhammad al-Shaybani).
The riwaya must be authentically attributed to Abu Hanifa and adopted by at least one other major imam.
3
Examine the example
The case of tayammum for one who soaked dates in water illustrates the exception: a riwaya from Abu Hanifa states that soaking dates invalidates wudu, and the Sahibayn adopted this view.
Thus the mufti follows the adopted riwaya, not the well-known view.
4
Apply the rule
Given a scenario in ibadat, first identify Imam Abu Hanifa's known position, then check if a riwaya from him adopted by another imam exists. If yes, follow the riwaya; otherwise, follow the known position.
This rule only applies to ibadat chapters, not muamalat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهَهُنَا ضَوَابِطُ مُحَرَّرَةً ٤٠ غَدَتْ لَدَى أَهْلِ النُّهَى مُقَرَّرَهُ فِي كُلِّ أَبْوَابِ الْعِبَادَاتِ رُبِّحُ القَوْلُ الإِمَامِ مُطْلَقاً مَا لَمْ تَصِحُ ـهُ رِوَايَةٌ بِهَا الْغَيْرُ أَخَذَ ٤٢ مِثْلُ تَيَهُم لِمَنْ تَمُرًا نَبَذُ
And here are precise controls that are established among the people of discernment: In all chapters of worship, the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is given preference absolutely, as long as there is not proven a narration from him which another (Imam) has taken - like the case of tayammum for one who has soaked dates in water.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule for muftis: in matters of worship (ibadat), the default is to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion without exception. However, if there exists a riwaya (transmission) from Abu Hanifa himself that conflicts with his well-known view and that riwaya has been adopted by other major Hanafi imams (like Abu Yusuf or Muhammad), then the mufti should follow that adopted riwaya. The example given is the case of a person who has soaked dates in water: according to Abu Hanifa's well-known view, this does not break wudu, but a riwaya from him states it does, and the Sahibayn adopted that view. In that instance, the mufti would follow the adopted riwaya. This rule is from the discipline of rasm al-mufti, guiding how to navigate internal Hanafi ikhtilaf in ibadat.

Key Terms
الإِمَامِ (al-Imām): Refers to Abu Hanifa, the founder of the Hanafi school.
ضَوَابِطُ (ḍawābiṭ): Plural of ḍābiṭ: precise controls or rules that govern the mufti's selection of opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In ibadat, the mufti follows Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion unless a proven riwaya from him has been adopted by another imam.

The Rule for Qada: Preferring Abu Yusuf
First rule: Abu Yusuf for qada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred authority for qada matters and apply the rule when selecting a Hanafi opinion for a judicial scenario.

Core Idea
For every judicial branch, Abu Yusuf's opinion is selected.

This lesson introduces the first of four rasm al-mufti rules: the preference for Imam Abu Yusuf's views in matters related to the judiciary (qada). As a mufti, you must know that different topics within the Hanafi school have different preferred authorities. Abu Yusuf's extensive experience as chief judge makes his opinion the default for qada issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject Matter
Determine if the case is judicial (qada) in nature – e.g., court procedures, evidence, judge qualifications, or rulings that a judge would issue.
Qada includes both the act of judging and the rules directly applied by a judge.
2
Recall the Rule
The passage states: 'كُلُّ فَرْعٍ بِالْقَضَاءِ تَعَلَّقَا قَوْلُ أَبِي يُوسُفَ فِيهِ يُنْتَقَى' – every branch related to qada, Abu Yusuf's saying is chosen.
This is an exception to the general Hanafi hierarchy (normally Abu Hanifa first).
3
Apply the Rule
When issuing a fatwa on a qada matter, give precedence to Abu Yusuf's view over other Hanafi opinions, unless a later tarjih overrides.
Know that Abu Yusuf’s riwayah holds special weight here due to his judicial practice.

The Rule for Dhawi al-Arham: Following Muhammad al-Shaybani
Second rule: Muhammad for dhawi al-arham

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that for issues of dhawi al-arham (uterine relatives), the fatwa is given according to Muhammad al-Shaybani, and apply this rule in inheritance fatwas.

Core Idea
In inheritance of uterine relatives, Muhammad's view is the fatwa basis.

This lesson covers the second rasm al-mufti rule: for matters regarding dhawi al-arham (relatives through females), the mufti should follow the opinion of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. This is a specific area where the later authoritative tarjih differs from the general preference for Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject as Dhawi al-Arham
Determine if the inheritance case involves a relative connected through a female link (e.g., maternal uncle, daughter's son, sister's daughter).
Dhawi al-arham are non-agnate relatives. In Hanafi inheritance, they inherit only when there are no male agnates (asabah) and no Quranic heirs.
2
Recall the Rule
The passage says: 'وَفِي مَسَائِلِ ذَوِي الْأَرْحَامِ قَدْ أَفْتَوْا بِمَا يَقُولُهُ مُحَمَّدُ' – in the issues of dhawi al-arham, they issued fatwa with what Muhammad says.
'They' refers to the later Hanafi authorities (mutakhkhirun) who established this tarjih.
3
Apply the Rule
When giving a fatwa on inheritance distribution involving dhawi al-arham, give priority to Muhammad al-Shaybani's opinion over those of Abu Hanifa or Abu Yusuf.
This rule is specific to this subset; for general inheritance (asabah), the regular hierarchy applies.

The Rule for Istihsan: Preferring Istihsan over Qiyas
Third rule: istihsan over qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that istihsan is preferred over qiyas in the Hanafi school, except for specific issues, and identify when the exception applies.

Core Idea
Istihsan (juristic preference) generally overrides qiyas, with known exceptions.

This lesson presents the third rasm rule: the mufti prefers rulings based on istihsan (juristic preference) over those based on qiyas (strict analogy). Istihsan is a recognized source in the Hanafi school that allows departure from qiyas for a stronger reason. However, there are exceptional cases where qiyas is retained.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Conflict
In a given case, check if there is a difference between the ruling from qiyas and the ruling from istihsan.
Qiyas is strict analogy; istihsan may be based on custom, necessity, or another stronger evidence.
2
Recall the General Rule
The passage says: 'اسْتِحْسَانَهُمْ عَلَى الْقِيَاسِ' – they preferred their istihsan over qiyas, 'إِلَّا مَسَائِلَ' – except for certain issues.
The exception phrase is somewhat unclear due to OCR; it may refer to the 'issues of al-Abbas' or be a corruption. In any case, exceptions are known in the school.
3
Apply the Preference
As a mufti, when both qiyas and istihsan are available, adopt the istihsan ruling unless the case falls within an exception where qiyas must be followed.
The exceptions are limited and should be learned from the manuals of usul (e.g., exceptions related to certain contracts or fixed transactions).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Fourth: the rulings of Zahir al-Riwaya (the well-known transmitted texts of the school) are binding and cannot be abandoned for an opposing opinion as long as they are transmitted. These rules help the mufti navigate the internal Hanafi hierarchy across different chapters of fiqh.

Key Terms
اسْتِحْسَان (Istihsān): Juristic preference, a method of departing from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling.
الْقِيَاس (al-Qiyās): Analogical reasoning, a method to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Rule for Zahir al-Riwaya: Binding Authority
Fourth rule: Zahir al-Riwaya is binding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that Zahir al-Riwaya rulings are binding and cannot be departed from in favor of conflicting opinions, as long as the transmission is sound.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwaya is the highest authority; deviation is not allowed when transmitted.

This lesson presents the fourth and most critical rasm rule: the corpus of Zahir al-Riwaya (the six core books of Imam Muhammad) holds supreme authority. The mufti cannot abandon a ruling found in these texts for a contrary opinion, because these transmissions are well-established. This ensures stability and consistency in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Source Level
Determine whether the ruling in question is found in the Zahir al-Riwaya works of Imam Muhammad.
These are: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat.
2
Apply the Rule of Non-Deviation
If the ruling is in Zahir al-Riwaya, it must be adopted; it is not permissible to follow an opposing view from other narrations (nawadir) or from the views of other Hanafi imams.
Exception: if there is a clear abrogation (naskh) or if the ruling contradicts a stronger dalil (Quran/Sunnah), but that is rare.
3
Confirm Transmission Reliability
The rule only applies if the transmission is authentic and uncontested. If there is doubt about the riwaya, further investigation is needed.
The passage says 'إِذْ يُنْقَلُ' – when it is transmitted (i.e., reliably).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Second: in inheritance cases for dhawi al-arham (relatives connected through females), the mufti gives fatwa according to Muhammad al-Shaybani. Fourth: the rulings of Zahir al-Riwaya (the well-known transmitted texts of the school) are binding and cannot be abandoned for an opposing opinion as long as they are transmitted. These rules help the mufti navigate the internal Hanafi hierarchy across different chapters of fiqh.

Key Terms
ظَاهِرُ الرِّوَايَةِ (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The apparent/well-known transmitted rulings in the school, referring to the six core books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Rasm al-Mufti: Preferred Opinions in Qada, Dhawil Arham, and Istihsan
Verses with commentary on preferring specific Hanafi imams' opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the preferred Hanafi imam for qada and dhawil arham cases, and apply the rule that istihsan takes precedence over qiyas except for specific exceptions, while adhering to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
For qada follow Abu Yusuf; for dhawil arham follow Muhammad; prefer istihsan over qiyas and Zahir al-Riwayah over weaker narrations.

This passage from Naseem al-Mufti presents four key principles (rasm al-mufti) that guide a Hanafi mufti in selecting which opinion to give as fatwa. These rules are based on the expertise of the early imams and the authority of the transmitted texts. Understanding these rules is essential for issuing correct fatwas within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify each rasm rule by its domain
Read the Arabic and translation to locate the four domains: judicial matters (qada), inheritance of distant relatives (dhawil arham), general conflict between istihsan and qiyas, and the binding authority of Zahir al-Riwayah.
The Persian couplets summarise the rules.
2
Match the domain to the preferred imam
For qada, the text selects Abu Yusuf. For dhawil arham, it selects Muhammad al-Shaybani. Note the reasons (Abu Yusuf's judicial experience, Muhammad's expertise in inheritance).
These are exceptions to the general rule that Abu Hanifa's view is primary.
3
Understand the general preference for istihsan
The text states that fuqaha preferred istihsan over qiyas, except for a few known exceptions. This is a broader methodological principle.
The exceptions are limited and well-known.
4
Recognise the supremacy of Zahir al-Riwayah
Once a ruling is established in the six authoritative books, one cannot deviate to a contrary narration, even if it exists. This ensures consistency in fatwa.
This rule is fundamental in Hanafi ifta methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ فَرُعِ بِالْقَضَا تَعَلَّقَا ۴۳ قَوْلُ أَبِى يُوسُفَ فِيهِ يُنتَقَى وَفِي مَسَائِلِ ذَوِى الْأَرْحَامِ، قَدْ ۴۴ أَفْتَوُا بِمَا يَقُولُهُ مُحَمَّدُ وَرَبَّحُوا اسْتِحْسَانَهُمْ عَلَى الْقِيَاسِ ۴۵ إِلَّا مَسَائِلَ، وَمَا فِيهَا الْعِبَاسُ ظَاهِرُ الْمَرُوقٌ، لَيْسَ يُعْدَلُ ٤٦ عَنْهُ إلَى خِلَافِهِ، إِذْ يُنْقَلُ ترجمہ: اور ہر وہ جزئیہ جس کا قضاء سے تعلق ہے اس میں امام ابو یوسف کا قول مختار ہے، اور ذوی الارحام کے مسائل میں فقہاء نے امام محمد کے قول پر فتوی دیا ہے، اور فقہاء نے قیاسی مسائل پر استحسان والے قول کو راجح قرار دیا ہے سوائے چند مسائل کے، اور ان مسائل میں کوئی اشتباہ نہیں ہے، اور ظاہر الروایہ سے اس کے مخالف قول کی طرف عدول نہیں کیا جائے گا جب اس کے خلاف دوسری روایت منقول ہو۔
جن مسئلوں کا ہوگا امر قضاء سے رشتہ ان میں تو بس چلے گا یعقوب ہی کا فتوی
ارحام کی بٹے گی میراث کس طرح سے ہیں معتبر بس اس میں ابن حسن کے فتوی
ترک قیاس کر کے مستحسن ہی کو لیجئے کچھ مسئلے ہیں ایسے جن میں خلاف کیجئے
And every branch related to judicial matters, the saying of Abu Yusuf is selected therein. And in matters of dhawil arham, they gave fatwa by what Muhammad said, and they preferred their istihsan over qiyas except for certain matters, and there is no confusion in them. The manifest [narration] is not to be deviated from to its opposite, since it is transmitted. Translation: And every case connected to judiciary, the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf is chosen. In inheritance of distant relatives, scholars gave fatwa according to Imam Muhammad's saying. They preferred istihsan over qiyas except for a few cases, and there is no ambiguity in those. And one should not deviate from Zahir al-Riwayah to a contrary narration, if a different transmission is reported against it. The Persian couplets: In matters connected to judiciary, only Ya'qub's fatwa applies. For dividing inheritance of dhawil arham, Ibn Hasan's fatwa is reliable. Abandon qiyas and adopt the preferred istihsan; there are some cases where you may differ.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents several key rasm rules for a Hanafi mufti. First, in matters related to qada (judicial proceedings), the preferred saying is that of Imam Abu Yusuf. This is because he had vast experience as a chief judge. Second, in cases of inheritance for dhawil arham (distant relatives who are not Quranic heirs nor agnates), the fatwa is given according to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Third, in general, when a ruling based on istihsan (juristic preference) contradicts qiyas (analogy), the istihsan view is given precedence, except for a few well-known exceptions. Fourth, a fatwa must be based on the Zahir al-Riwayah (the six authoritative compilations of Imam Muhammad) and cannot be overridden by a weaker narration, even if such a narration exists. The Persian couplets reinforce these rules: judicial matters follow Abu Yusuf, dhawil arham inheritance follows Muhammad, and istihsan is preferred over qiyas except for specific cases.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Judicial proceedings, court cases
ذوی الأرحام (dhawil arham): Distant relatives who are neither Quranic heirs nor agnates
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that sets aside strict analogy in favor of a more suitable ruling
ظاهر الروایة (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six authoritative books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing the established Hanafi positions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a case that involves judicial proceedings (qada), which imam's qawl is preferred according to this rasm rule?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad
D) All equally

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti must follow domain-specific rasm rules: for qada follow Abu Yusuf, for dhawil arham follow Muhammad, prefer istihsan over qiyas, and never deviate from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
Three Rasm al-Mufti Principles: Dirayah, Takfir Avoidance, and Ruju'
Three rasm al-mufti rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply three rasm al-mufti rules: (1) retaining reasoning supported by transmission, (2) preferring weak hadith that negates kufr, and (3) treating a mujtahid's retraction as abrogation.

Core Idea
The mufti must uphold reasoning supported by tradition, avoid takfir even with weak evidence, and abandon any opinion its author has rescinded.

This passage presents three foundational principles for the mufti's methodology (rasm al-mufti). They guide how a mufti should balance reasoning (dirayah) and transmission (riwayah), how to weigh narrations that protect a Muslim's faith status, and how to handle a mujtahid's change of opinion. Understanding these rules prevents common errors in fatwa issuance, especially in sensitive matters like takfir and reliance on authoritative positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three separate rules
Read the Arabic and translation to distinguish three distinct principles: (a) dirayah with riwayah, (b) weak hadith negating kufr, (c) the effect of a mujtahid's ruju'. Each is marked by 'وَ' or a break in the text.
The Persian couplets reinforce these rules.
2
Analyse the first rule: Do not abandon sound reasoning when a narration supports it
Understand that if the mufti's own ijtihad (dirayah) yields a ruling, and a transmitted report (riwayah) agrees with it, the mufti must not abandon his reasoning. This encourages confidence in sound ijtihad corroborated by textual evidence.
This rule prevents the mufti from discarding his own well-reasoned opinion simply because a different or isolated report appears.
3
Analyse the second rule: Prefer any narration that negates kufr from a Muslim, even if weak
The mufti must give precedence to any report, however weak in terms of authenticity, that absolves a Muslim from disbelief. This reflects the Hanafi principle of caution (ihtiyat) in matters of takfir.
This does not apply to other areas of fiqh; it is a specific rule for cases where a person's Islamic status is at stake.
4
Analyse the third rule: Treat a mujtahid's retracted opinion as abrogated
If a qualified mujtahid explicitly withdraws his earlier opinion, that opinion loses its authority entirely, similar to a mansukh (abrogated) ruling. The mufti must follow the later, unretracted opinion.
This ensures that fatwas are based on the most mature and final reasoning of the authority.
5
Apply the rules to hypothetical fatwa scenarios
Consider cases: (a) the mufti's own qiyas suggests a ruling, and a marfu' hadith supports it; (b) a weak mursal hadith says a person is not a kafir; (c) Imam Abu Hanifa's later position differs from an earlier one. Decide the mufti's course.
These are classic situations covered by the principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يَنبَغِى الْعُدُولُ عَنْ دِرَايَهُ ٤٧ إِذَا أَتَى بِوَفُقِهَا رِوَايَهُ وَكُلُّ قَوْلِ جَاءَ يَنْفِي الْكُفْرًا ۲۸ عَنْ مُسْلِمٍ، وَلَوْ ضَعِيفاً أَحْرَى وَكُلُّ مَا رَجَعَ عَنْهُ المُجْتَهِد و صَارَ كَمَنْسُوخ فَغَيْرُهُ اعْتُمِد ترجمہ: اور دلیل سے عدول کرنا مناسب نہیں ہے جب کہ اس کے موافق کوئی روایت بھی ہو، اور ہر ایسا قول جو مسلم سے کفر کی نفی کرتا ہوا گر چہ وہ ضعیف ہو قبول کرنے کے زیادہ لائق ہے، اور ہر وہ قول جس سے مجتہد نے رجوع کر لیا ہے وہ گویا منسوخ ہو گیا ہے، پس اس کے علاوہ قول پر اعتماد کیا جائے گا۔
معقول ہے درایت وابستہ ہے روایت اس کو نہ چھوڑیں ہر گز کہتی ہے یہ درایت
اور ایسا قول جس سے منفی ہو کفر مسلم گو وہ ضعیف تر ہو تسلیم کرلے عالم
فتوی نہ کفر کا دے روکے زباں کو اپنی جو کہہ گئے مشائخ مانے ہر ایک مفتی
فتوے سے مجتہد جب اپنے رجوع کرلے مرجوع فیصلہ کو منسوخ ہی وہ مانے
It is not appropriate to deviate from a sound reasoning (dirayah) when a transmission (riwayah) comes in agreement with it. And every saying that negates kufr from a Muslim, even if weak, is more worthy of acceptance. And every saying from which the mujtahid has retracted becomes like abrogated, so other than it is relied upon. Translation: It is not proper to abandon a rational opinion when a narration supports it. And any statement that removes the charge of kufr from a Muslim, even if it is a weak narration, is more deserving of acceptance. And any opinion from which the mujtahid himself has recanted is like an abrogated ruling; so the other opinion is relied upon. The Persian couplets: Sound reasoning is connected to tradition; never abandon it. Accept a statement that negates kufr of a Muslim, even if it is weak. The scholar should not issue a fatwa of kufr, but restrain his tongue; whatever the mashayikh said, every mufti follows. When a mujtahid has retracted his own fatwa, consider the retracted ruling as abrogated.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage provides three additional rasm rules for issuing fatwa. First, if a mufti's own reasoning (dirayah) leads to a ruling, and there is a transmitted narration (riwayah) that supports it, the mufti should not abandon the reasoning. In other words, a sound rational opinion that is corroborated by textual evidence must be upheld. Second, if a narration, even if weak, negates the charge of disbelief (kufr) from a Muslim, it should be given preference. This shows the Hanafi emphasis on preserving a Muslim's status; it is better to err in declaring someone a believer than to wrongly declare them a disbeliever. Third, if a mujtahid (a qualified jurist) has explicitly retracted his own earlier opinion, that earlier opinion loses its authority, much like a mansukh (abrogated) ruling. The mufti must then follow the later, retentive opinion. The Persian couplets summarize: hold fast to reasoning supported by tradition; accept weak hadith that avoids takfir; and when a mujtahid recants, treat his old view as null.

Key Terms
درایة (dirayah): Reasoning, intellectual understanding, or sound legal reasoning of a mujtahid
روایة (riwayah): A transmitted narration, usually from the Prophet or Companions
كفر (kufr): Disbelief; declaring a Muslim an apostate
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a ruling that is no longer valid
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction; the act of a mujtahid abandoning his earlier opinion

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what should a mufti do if a mujtahid has retracted his own earlier opinion?
A) Follow the earlier opinion out of respect for the mujtahid
B) Follow the later opinion because the earlier one becomes like abrogated
C) Choose the opinion that is easier for the people
D) Ask a different mujtahid for a new fatwa

Key Takeaway
The mufti must not abandon sound reasoning supported by transmission, must give precedence to even weak narrations that negate takfir, and must treat a mujtahid's retracted opinion as null.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Rules of Preferring Dirayah and Riwayah in Fatwa
Stating rules for preferring reason-aligned transmissions and accepting weak narrations that negate kufr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the three Hanafi rules for preferring dirayah and riwayah in fatwa and construct a fatwa hierarchy using them.

Core Idea
A weak narration that negates kufr is accepted over a stronger one that affirms it.

The Hanafi mufti is not merely a transmitter of narrations; he must exercise juridical reasoning (dirayah) while respecting transmitted reports (riwayah). This lesson introduces three key principles from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti that guide the mufti's preference when faced with conflicting evidence or when an earlier ruling has been retracted. Understanding these rules is essential for sound fatwa construction within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rules
The passage contains three distinct maxims: (1) do not abandon dirayah when a riwayah agrees with it; (2) accept weak narrations that negate kufr; (3) treat a mujtahid's retraction like abrogation. List each in your own words.
These are the foundational rules for tarjih in fatwa.
2
Understand the principle behind each rule
The first rule balances reason and transmission. The second rule reflects caution (ihtiyat) in matters of faith. The third rule ensures that later, more refined opinions are followed. For each rule, articulate the underlying wisdom.
The second rule is unique because it overrides the usual weakness criterion.
3
Apply the rules to a fatwa scenario
Given a scenario where a weak hadith says something does not constitute kufr, while a stronger hadith says it does, the mufti should prefer the weak hadith because it negates kufr. Construct a brief fatwa draft.
This application shows the hierarchy in practice.
4
Recognize the hierarchy implications
When a mujtahid retracts an opinion, that earlier opinion loses authority; the later opinion becomes the mufta bihi. Identify how this rule impacts the reliability of earlier fatwas.
This rule prevents muftis from relying on outdated positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ: اور دلیل سے عدول کرنا مناسب نہیں ہے جب کہ اس کے موافق کوئی روایت بھی ہو، اور ہر ایسا قول جو مسلم سے کفر کی نفی کرتا ہو اگر چہ وہ ضعیف ہو قبول کرنے کے زیادہ لائق ہے، اور ہر وہ قول جس سے مجتہد نے رجوع کر لیا ہے وہ گویا منسوخ ہو گیا ہے، پس اس کے علاوہ قول پر اعتماد کیا جائے گا۔
معقول ہے درایت وابستہ ہے روایت اس کو نہ چھوڑیں ہر گز کہتی ہے یہ درایت

فتوی نہ کفر کا دے روکے زباں کو اپنی جو کہہ گئے مشائخ مانے ہر ایک مفتی
فتوے سے مجتہد جب اپنے رجوع کرلے مرجوع فیصلہ کو منسوخ ہی وہ مانے
It is not appropriate to deviate from reasoning (diraayah) when a transmission (riwaayah) comes in agreement with it. And every statement that negates disbelief from a Muslim, even if weak, is more deserving. And every statement from which the mujtahid has retracted becomes like abrogated, so reliance is on other than it.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage, from a commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, lays down three key principles for the Hanafi mufti. First, do not abandon a reasoned juristic opinion (diraayah) if it is supported by a transmitted report (riwaayah). Second, when there is a weak narration that negates disbelief (kufr) from a Muslim, it is to be accepted out of caution, even if weak. Third, when a mujtahid (imam) retracts from his earlier opinion, that earlier opinion is treated like an abrogated (mansukh) ruling, and the later opinion is followed. These rules reflect the Hanafi emphasis on combining reason with transmission and the principle of ikhtiyar.

Key Terms
دراية (diraayah): Juridical reasoning or acumen arrived at independently through ijtihad.
رواية (riwaayah): A transmitted report, typically from the founding imams.
رجوع (ruju'): The act of a mujtahid retracting his earlier opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) It is accepted as more deserving.
D) It is accepted only if there is no stronger proof.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa practice, weak narrations that negate kufr are preferred over stronger ones, and retracted opinions are treated as abrogated.

Hierarchy of Hanafi Sources: Mutun, Shuruh, and Fatawa
Defining the order of preference among Hanafi textual sources: mutun, then shuruh, then old fatawa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchy of Hanafi textual sources (mutun, shuruh, fatawa) to determine the most preponderant ruling in a given fatwa scenario, and identify when an explicit correction overrides the default order.

Core Idea
Mutun have implicit tarjih over shuruh, and shuruh over old fatawa, unless an explicit correction exists.

This lesson introduces a foundational rasm al-mufti rule: the order of preference among Hanafi written sources. A mufti must know which text takes precedence when rulings differ. The passage establishes a hierarchy: mutun (concise authoritative texts) are most preferred, then shuruh (commentaries), then old fatawa (fatwa collections). However, there are important exceptions, such as explicit corrections and the special treatment of certain works like Fatawa al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default hierarchy
From the first verse, extract the three levels: mutun > shuruh > old fatawa. Note that this default applies 'as long as there is no other statement that has been explicitly corrected.'
The term 'old fatawa' refers to earlier fatwa collections, not later ones.
2
Understand the exception for explicit correction
If a later text explicitly corrects the wording of a mutun, the corrected wording takes precedence. This is the key exception to the default hierarchy.
Explicit correction (tasrih) overrides implicit tarjih.
3
Recognize special cases: sabiq al-aqwal
Within Fatawa al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhar, the earlier opinions (sabiq al-aqwal) are given precedence. Outside these works, the later opinion (mu'akhkhar) with clear evidence is followed.
This distinction reflects the high reliability of these two works.
4
Apply the principle of mu'akhkhar
In works like al-Hidayah, the later opinion that comes with evidence (dalil) is the refined (muharrar) ruling. This is the standard in many later Hanafi texts.
The later opinion is not always preferred; it must be accompanied by strong evidence.
5
Practice tarjih in a scenario
Given a conflict between a matn and a later fatwa with evidence but no explicit correction, decide which ruling to follow. Use the default hierarchy and then check for exceptions.
Always verify whether the matn has been explicitly corrected.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ قَوْلٍ فِي الْمُتُونِ الْبِنَا فَذَاكَ تَرْجِيحٌ لَهُ ضِمْنًا أَنَى فَرُجْحَةُ الْمُتُونِ عَلَى الشُّرُوحِ وَالشُّرُوحُ عَلَى الْفَتَاوَى الْقِدْمِ مِنْ ذَاتِ رُجُوحٍ مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ سِوَاهُ لَفْظًا صُحِّحَا فَالْأَرْجَحُ الَّذِي بِهِ قَدْ صُرِّحًا
وَسَابِقُ الْأَقْوَالِ فِي الْخَانِيَةِ وَمُلْتَقَى الْأَبْحُرِ ذُو مَزِيَّةٍ وَفِي سِوَاهُمَا اعْتُمِدَ مَا أَخَّرُوا دَلِيلَهُ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُحَرَّرُ كَمَا هُوَ الْعَادَةُ فِي الْهَدَايَةِ وَنَحْوِهَا لِرَاجِحِ الدِّرَايَةِ كَذَا إِذَا مَا وَاحِدًا قَدْ عَلَّلُوا لَهُ وَتَعْلِيلَ سِوَاهُ أَهْمَلُوا
ترجمہ: اور ہر وہ قول جس کو متون میں لیا گیا ہے تو یہ اس قول کی ضمن ترجیح ہے جو اس کو حاصل ہوگئی ہے، پس ترجیح دی جائے گی متون کو شروح پر اور شروح کو قدیم فتاوی پر ، یہ ترجیح اصحاب الترجیح کی جانب سے ہے، جب تک متون کے علاوہ قول کی صراحتا صحیح نہ کی گئی ہو، ورنہ وہ قول زیادہ رائج ہوگا جس کی صراحا صحیح کی گئی ہے۔ مذکور متن ہونا تصحیح ہے مسلم
اس پہلو سے ہوئی ہیں شرحوں پہ یہ مقدم
متن اور شروح و فتوی ترتیب ان میں رکھیں متن آپ پہلے دیکھیں پھر شرح و فتوی دیکھیں
تصحیح متن کو بھی ضمنی ہی آپ جانیں جب ہو کہیں مصرح تقدیم اس کی چاہیں
ترجمہ: اور فتاوی قاضی خان اور ملتقی الا بحر میں پہلے بیان کئے ہوئے اقوال فضیلت رکھنے والے ہیں، اور ان دونوں کتابوں کے علاوہ میں اس قول پر اعتماد کیا جائے گا جس کی دلیل فقہاء بعد میں بیان کریں، کیوں کہ وہی قول تنقیح شدہ ہوتا ہے، جیسا کہ ہدایہ اور اس کے ہم مرتبہ کتب میں عادت ہے۔
And every statement that is in the mutun (matn texts), then that is an implicit tarjih for it. So mutun have preference over shuruh, and shuruh over the old fatawa from the people of tarjih, as long as there is no other statement that has been explicitly corrected. Then the most preponderant is that which has been explicitly stated. And the earlier opinions in Fatawa al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhar have excellence. And besides these two, rely on what the later [scholars] have advanced their evidence, because it is the refined [opinion], as is the custom in Hidayah and its ilk for preponderance of reasoning. Likewise, when they have given a ta'lil for one [opinion] and omitted the ta'lil for another.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents a hierarchical preference for Hanafi fatwa sources. The first verse establishes that opinions recorded in the authoritative mutun (such as Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Kanz al-Daqa'iq) carry an implicit tarjih over commentaries (shuruh), and commentaries over old fatwa collections, unless there is an explicit correction in a later text. The second verse notes that within specific works like Fatawa al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhar, the earlier opinions (sabiq al-aqwal) have precedence. Outside these, the later opinion (mu'akhkhar) that comes with clear evidence is to be followed, as is the practice in Hidayah, where the refined ruling is given. This reflects the Hanafi principle of 'i'timad 'ala al-mu'akhkhar (reliance on the later) when accompanied by evidence.

Key Terms
متون (mutun): Authoritative abridged texts of Hanafi fiqh, like al-Quduri, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, etc.
شروح (shuruh): Commentaries on the mutun, such as al-Lubab or al-Hidayah.
الخانية (al-Khaniyah): Fatawa al-Khaniyya, a famous fatwa collection by Qadi al-Khan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fatawa al-Khaniyya always takes precedence.
B) The later opinion with evidence (like in Hidayah) always takes precedence.
C) Fatawa al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhar have precedence for their early opinions, but outside those, later opinions with evidence are followed.
D) No hierarchy exists; all are equal.

Key Takeaway
The hierarchy of Hanafi sources ensures consistency in fatwa: mutun first, then shuruh, then old fatawa, with explicit corrections and the later-with-evidence principle as key refinements.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
8 min
Hierarchy of Hanafi Fatwa Sources: Mutun, Shuruh, and Fatawa
Establishes hierarchy and preference rules for fatwa sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchy of mutun, shuruh, and fatawa to determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling) when multiple sources exist.

Core Idea
Mutun precede shuruh, shuruh precede old fatwas—unless a statement is explicitly corrected; then that corrected statement is mu'tamad.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, a mufti must navigate multiple sources of the madhhab. This passage from Naseem al-Mufti lays out the rules for tarjih (preference) among these sources. Understanding these rules ensures that fatwas are based on the most authoritative positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify source types
Recognize whether a ruling comes from a matn (core text), a sharh (commentary), or a fatwa collection (fatawa qadima).
Mutun include works like al-Mukhtasar, al-Wiqayah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Apply default hierarchy
Mutun take precedence over shuruh, and shuruh over old fatwa collections.
This is the general rule; exceptions follow.
3
Check for tasheeh
If a source outside the mutun is explicitly declared sahih (corrected), that corrected statement overrides the default hierarchy.
Tasheeh is a tool used by later scholars to refine the madhhab.
4
Apply book-specific rules
In Fatawa Qadikhan and Multaqa al-Abhur, earlier statements are preferred. In other works, the later statement (with its proof) is relied upon.
Al-Hidayah is an example where the later statement is often mu'tamad.
5
Consider ta'lil
If a legal cause (illa) is given for one qawl and not for another, the qawl with ta'lil is preferred.
Ta'lil signals that the jurist has deliberately chosen that ruling.

صُحْحَا ۵۲ فَالْأَرْجَحُ الَّذِي بِهِ قَدْ صُرِّحًا ترجمہ: اور ہر وہ قول جس کو متون میں لیا گیا ہے تو یہ اس قول کی ضمن ترجیح ہے جو اس کو حاصل ہوگئی ہے، پس ترجیح دی جائے گی متون کو شروح پر اور شروح کو قدیم فتاوی پر ، یہ ترجیح اصحاب الترجیح کی جانب سے ہے، جب تک متون کے علاوہ قول کی صراحتا صحیح نہ کی گئی ہو، ورنہ وہ قول زیادہ رائج ہوگا جس کی صراحا صحیح کی گئی ہے۔ مذکور متن ہونا تصحیح ہے مسلم اس پہلو سے ہوئی ہیں شرحوں پہ یہ مقدم متن اور شروح و فتوی ترتیب ان میں رکھیں متن آپ پہلے دیکھیں پھر شرح و فتوی دیکھیں تصحیح متن کو بھی ضمنی ہی آپ جانیں جب ہو کہیں مصرح تقدیم اس کی چاہیں وَسَابِقُ الْأقْوَالِ فِى الْخَانِيَه ۵۳ وَمُلْتَقَى الْأَبْحُرِ ذُو مَزِيَّهُ وَفِي سِوَاهُمَا اعْتُمِدَ مَا أَخَّرُوا ۵٤ دَلِيلَهُ لأَنَّهُ المُحَرَّرُ كَمَا هُوَ الْعَادَةُ فِى الْهَدَايَه ۵۵ وَنَحْوِهَا لِرَاجِحَ الدِّرَايَهُ كَذَا إِذَا مَا وَاحِداً قَدْ عَلَّلُوا ۵۶ لَهُ، وَتَعْلِيْلَ سِوَاهُ أَهْمَلُوا ترجمہ: اور فتاوی قاضی خان اور ملتقی الا بحر میں پہلے بیان کئے ہوئے اقوال فضیلت رکھنے والے ہیں، اور ان دونوں کتابوں کے علاوہ میں اس قول پر اعتماد کیا جائے گا جس کی دلیل فقہاء بعد میں بیان کریں، کیوں کہ وہی قول تنقیح شدہ ہوتا ہے، جیسا کہ ہدایہ اور اس جیسی کتابوں میں یہی طریقہ ہے دلیل کے اعتبار سے راجح قول کے لئے ، اسی طرح جب فقہاء ایک قول کی علت بیان کریں اور اس کے علاوہ دوسرے قول کی علت نہ بیان کریں۔ فتوے کی جو کتب ہیں معمول ان کا یہ ہے لکھتے ہیں خانیہ ہیں خانیہ میں مفتی یہ کو بہ پہلے حلبی کا ملتقی میں مفتی معمول بھی یہی ہے جو ہوگا لکھیں گے اس کو پہلے ان دو کے ماسوا ہیں فتوے کی جو کتابیں معمول ان کتب کا ہے مختلف یہ سمجھیں کرتے ہیں وہ مدلل آخر میں معتمد کو ایسی کتب میں فتوی آخر کے قول پر ہو تنقیح اس طرح سے ہو جاتی ہے نمایاں اور بات کا سمجھنا ہوتا ہے سب کو آساں کا سانی مرغینانی کا ہے یہی طریقہ مختار قول ان کا آخر میں ہی رہے مدلل اور ہوتا ہے کبھی یہ کرتے ہیں وہ بس قول معتمد کو باقی کو کر کے مہمل گا وَحَيْثُمَا وَجَدْتَ قَوْلَيْن ، وَقَدْ ۵۷ صُحْحَ وَاحِدٌ، فَذَاكَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ بِنَحْوِ ذَا الْفَتْوَى عَلَيْهِ الْأَشْبَهُ ۵۸ وَالْأظْهَرِ الْمُخْتَارُ ذَا وَالْأَوْجَهُ الصَّحِيحُ وَالاصَحَ آكَدُ ۵۹ مِنْهُ، وَقِيلَ: عَكْسُهُ الْمُؤكَّدُ كَذَا بِهِ يُفْتَى عَلَيْهِ الْفَتُوى ٦٠ وَذَانِ مِنْ جَمِيعِ تِلْكَ أَقْوى
Every statement found in the texts (mutun) – that is an implicit preference given to it. So texts are given precedence over commentaries, and commentaries over old fatwas – this is a preference from the people of tarjih, unless a statement other than the text is explicitly corrected; then the one explicitly corrected is more authoritative. Earlier statements in al-Khaniyah and Multaqa al-Abhur have merit. In other than these two, reliance is on what the jurists mention later as its proof, because it is refined, as is customary in al-Hidayah and similar works for the more authoritative ruling. Likewise, when they give a cause (ta'lil) for one statement and neglect the cause for another. Whenever you find two statements and one is declared sahih (corrected), that is the mu'tamad (relied upon). On this basis, fatwa is given on the ashbah (most similar), azhar (most apparent), mukhtar (chosen), awjah (most appropriate), sahih (correct), and asahh (more correct) – the latter being more emphatic. It is said the opposite is mu'akkad (emphasized). Thus fatwa is given. And these two are the strongest of all those.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a set of rasm rules for muftis on how to determine the preferred ruling when there are multiple sources. It begins by establishing a hierarchy: mutun (core texts like al-Mukhtasar, al-Wiqayah) take precedence over shuruh (commentaries) and shuruh over fatawa qadima (old fatwa collections). This precedence is implicit unless a statement outside the mutun is explicitly declared sahih (correct) – then that statement takes precedence. Next, it addresses specific books: in Fatawa Qadikhan and Multaqa al-Abhur, the earlier statement is considered more meritorious. In other books, the later statement (with its proof) is relied upon because it is the refined (muharrar) position, as in al-Hidayah where the last mentioned qawl is often the mu'tamad. Additionally, if jurists provide a ta'lil (legal cause) for one statement and ignore another, the one with the cause is preferred. Finally, it explains that when one of two qawls is explicitly corrected (tasheeh), that becomes the mu'tamad. Terms like ashbah, azhar, mukhtar, awjah, sahih, asahh indicate degrees of strength, with asahh being more emphatic, though some say the opposite is mu'akkad. The mufti must apply these rules to issue fatwas correctly.

Key Terms
متون (mutun): Core authoritative texts of the Hanafi madhhab (e.g., al-Mukhtasar, al-Wiqayah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq)
تصحیح (tasheeh): The act of declaring a particular narration or ruling as sahih (correct) by later scholars
علت (ta'lil): Providing a legal cause (illa) for a ruling; a qawl with ta'lil is preferred over one without

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is given precedence: a statement from a sharh (commentary) or a statement from an old fatwa collection (fatawa qadima)?
A) Sharh is preferred.
B) Old fatwa is preferred.
C) They are equal.
D) It depends on the author.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must apply a hierarchy: mutun > shuruh > fatawa qadima, but explicit correction (tasheeh) overrides, and specific books have their own order for earlier/later statements.

Identifying the Mu'tamad When One Qawl Is Corrected
Explains the rule for preferring a corrected qawl using specific terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the terms of tashih in Hanafi fatwa literature and correctly determine which opinion is the mu'tamad based on their relative strength.

Core Idea
When two opinions exist, the one explicitly corrected (tashih) is the mu'tamad; the strongest indicators are 'bihi yufata' and 'alayhi al-fatwa'.

A mufti often encounters two conflicting narrations on a single issue. The later Hanafi scholars developed a clear system of 'tashih' to indicate which opinion is relied upon (mu'tamad). Recognizing these indicators and their hierarchy is essential for issuing correct fatwas. This lesson presents the rule and the key terms used in the manuals.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the rule
The passage states: whenever two opinions exist and one is corrected (suhhiha), that corrected opinion is the mu'tamad.
Suhhiha means the author or a later authority explicitly declared it sound.
2
List the tashih terms
Identify the eight terms mentioned: 'al-fatwa 'alayh', 'al-ashbah', 'al-azhar', 'al-mukhtar', 'al-awjah', 'al-sahih', 'al-asahh', and the phrases 'bihi yufata' and 'alayhi al-fatwa'.
The last two are listed separately and emphasized as strongest.
3
Understand the hierarchy
Note the relative strength: 'bihi yufata' and 'alayhi al-fatwa' are أَقْوَى (stronger) than all other terms. Among 'sahih' and 'asahh', the primary view is that 'asahh' is more emphatic (آكَد), though a minority reverses this.
The text does not rank the other five terms (ashbah, azhar, etc.) relative to each other.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given two opinions, one marked with a weaker term and the other with a stronger term, choose the one with the stronger indicator as the mu'tamad. If equally strong, further principles may apply.
Practice using the terms in context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَحَيْثُمَا وَجَدْتَ قَوْلَيْنِ، وَقَدْ صُحِّحَ وَاحِدٌ، فَذَاكَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ بِنَحْوِ: الْفَتْوَى عَلَيْهِ، الْأَشْبَهُ، الْأَظْهَرُ، الْمُخْتَارُ، الْأَوْجَهُ، الصَّحِيحُ، وَالْأَصَحُّ آكَدُ مِنْهُ، وَقِيلَ: عَكْسُهُ. كَذَاكَ بِهِ يُفْتَى وَعَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى، وَذَانِ مِنْ جَمِيعِ تِلْكَ أَقْوَى.
ترجمہ: اور جب آپ ایسے دو اقوال پائیں جن میں سے ایک قول کی تصحیح کی گئی ہو تو وہی قول معتمد ہوگا، (اس کی تصحیح کی گئی ہو) الْفَتْوَى عَلَيْهِ، الْأَشْبَهُ، الْأَظْهَرُ، الْمُخْتَارُ، اور الْأَوْجَهُ جیسے الفاظ سے، یا صَحِيح اور أَصَح کے الفاظ سے، اور أَصَح کا لفظ صَحِيح سے زیادہ مؤکد ہے، اور ایک قول یہ ہے کہ صَحِيح کا لفظ أَصَح سے زیادہ مؤکد ہے۔ اسی طرح تصحیح کی گئی ہو 
بِهِ يُفْتَى، يا عَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى سے، اور یہ دونوں الفاظ سابقہ تمام الفاظ سے زیادہ قوت والے ہیں۔
اور ہوں اگر کہیں پر دو قول مسئلے میں صحیح والا جو ہو فتویٰ اسی دیں، تصحیح کے مقرر الفاظ بھی تو سن لیں اور ان کا فرق باہم اچھی طرح سے سمجھیں: اس قول پر ہے فتویٰ، یہ قول حق سے اشبہ، قول تو ہے اظہر، مختار یہ، یہ اوجہ ہے، صحیح لکھیں یا یہ اصح ہے لکھیں، اور ہے اصح مؤکد، یہ بھی یہیں سمجھ لیں۔ یہ بھی کہا گیا ہے جس کو صحیح لکھیں ہے وہ اصح سے بہتر، فتویٰ اسی پہ دیں۔ صحیح کے لئے ہے لکھنا علیہ الفتویٰ (علیہ الفتویٰ) پہلے یہ لکھا ہو یفتی کا پھر ہو فقرہ (بہ یفتی)
And wherever you find two opinions, and one has been corrected, that is the relied-upon (mu'tamad), by way of: al-fatwa 'alayh, al-ashbah, al-azhar, al-mukhtar, al-awjah, al-sahih, and al-asahh is more emphatic than it, and it was said: the opposite. Likewise, 'bihi yufata' and 'alayhi al-fatwa', and these two are stronger than all of those. Translation: And when you find two opinions such that one of them has been corrected, that is the mu'tamad. It is corrected by words like: al-fatwa 'alayh, al-ashbah, al-azhar, al-mukhtar, and al-awjah, or by the words sahih and asahh. The word asahh is more emphatic than sahih, and one opinion is that sahih is more emphatic than asahh. Similarly, it is corrected by 'bihi yufata' or 'alayhi al-fatwa', and these two words are stronger than all the previous words. And if somewhere in a mas'ala there are two opinions, and the one that is sahih, give fatwa according to that; listen to the fixed words of tashih and understand their difference well: this qawl is the one for fatwa, this qawl is ashbah to the truth, this qawl is azhar, this is mukhtar, this is awjah, write sahih or write asahh, and asahh is emphatic, understand this here. It has also been said that that which is written as sahih is better than asahh, give fatwa based on it. For sahih, it is to write 'alayhi al-fatwa', and before that write 'bihi yufata', then the phrase 'bihi yufata'.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational rasm rule for muftis: when a fatwa book records two conflicting opinions on a matter, and one of them has been explicitly 'corrected' (tashih) by the author or later scholars, that corrected opinion becomes the mu'tamad (relied-upon) position for issuing fatwas. The passage then lists the key terms used to signal such tashih: 'al-fatwa 'alayh' (the fatwa is upon it), 'al-ashbah' (the more similar to the truth), 'al-azhar' (the more apparent), 'al-mukhtar' (the chosen), 'al-awjah' (the more proper), 'al-sahih' (the sound), and 'al-asahh' (the soundest). A critical nuance is the comparative strength of 'sahih' and 'asahh': the majority view is that 'asahh' is more emphatic, but a minority view reverses this. The passage also notes that the expressions 'bihi yufata' (by it fatwa is given) and 'alayhi al-fatwa' (upon it is the fatwa) are the strongest indicators of the mu'tamad. The Urdu commentary reinforces this hierarchy and practical usage, advising the mufti to understand the precise weight of each term and to give fatwa accordingly.

Key Terms
المعتمد (al-mu'tamad): The relied-upon opinion that should be used for issuing fatwas, indicated by tashih.
الأشبه (al-ashbah): The opinion that is more similar (to the truth or to the Hanafi principles), serving as an indicator of tashih.
الأظهر (al-azhar): The more apparent or manifest opinion, indicating it is preferred.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen opinion, indicating it is selected as the mu'tamad.
الأوجه (al-awjah): The more proper or correct opinion in the view of the author.
الصحيح (al-sahih): The sound opinion; one of the terms indicating tashih.
الأصح (al-asahh): The soundest opinion; considered more emphatic than 'sahih' according to the primary ruling.
به يفتى (bihi yufata): A phrase meaning 'by it fatwa is given', used as a strong indicator of the mu'tamad.
عليه الفتوى ('alayhi al-fatwa): A phrase meaning 'upon it is the fatwa', also a strong indicator of the mu'tamad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two expressions are considered the strongest indicators that an opinion is the mu'tamad?
A) al-ashbah and al-azhar
B) al-sahih and al-asahh
C) al-mukhtar and al-awjah
D) bihi yufata and 'alayhi al-fatwa

Key Takeaway
The mu'tamad is identified by tashih terms; 'bihi yufata' and 'alayhi al-fatwa' are the strongest, and 'asahh' is stronger than 'sahih'.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

Rule When Both Opinions Are Corrected: Balancing Discretion and Authority
Parsing rule for corrected opinions in fatwa methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a mufti has discretion between two corrected opinions and when he must follow the preferred opinion based on authority markers.

Core Idea
When both opinions are corrected, free choice is the baseline, but six authority markers override discretion.

In the Hanafi madhhab, when a later scholar corrects (sahhaha) a weaker opinion, it becomes mu'tamad. But what if both opposing opinions are corrected? This passage from Naseem al-Mufti provides the rule: the mufti may choose, except when one opinion has a specific marker of preponderance. Understanding these markers is essential for responsible fatwa-giving.

Guided Path
1
State the baseline rule
When both opinions are corrected, each is considered reliable and the mufti may choose either.
This gives the mufti freedom in cases of equivalent authority.
2
List the six exceptions
These are: 'sahih/asahh' distinction, 'bihi yufata', presence in mutun, being qawl al-Imam, being zahir al-marwi, and being the view of jull al-'izam.
Each exception indicates a higher level of authority.
3
Explain each exception's weight
For example, 'asahh' implies a stronger correction. 'Bihi yufata' is an explicit fatwa instruction. Mutun are the core texts. Qawl al-Imam is the founder's view. Zahir al-marwi is from the six works. Jull al-'izam indicates consensus of major scholars.
These form the hierarchy.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given two corrected opinions, check if any of these markers applies. If one matches, that opinion is mu'tamad and must be followed. If none, the mufti may choose.
The mufti should not rely on personal inclination but on these objective criteria.
5
Reflect on the wisdom of the rule
This rule balances consistency with flexibility: it permits choice when authorities are equal, but guides choice when the madhhab has a clear preference.
This ensures that fatwa remains within the madhhab's framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ تَجِدْ تَصْحِيْحَ قَوْلَيْنِ وَرَدْ فَاخْتَرْ لِمَا شِئْتَ، فَكُلُّ مُعْتَمَدْ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَا صَحِيحاً وَأَصَحَّ، أَوْ قِيلَ: ذَا يُفْتَى بِهِ فَقَدْ رَجَحْ، أَوْ كَانَ فِي الْمُتُونِ أَوْ قَوْلَ الْإِمَامِ، أَوْ ظَاهِرَ الْمَرْوِيِّ، أَوْ جُلَّ الْعِظَامِ.
And if you find that both opinions have been corrected and transmitted, then choose whichever you wish, for each is mu'tamad, except when they are sahih and asahh, or it is said: 'this one gives fatwa by it' so it has preponderance, or it is in the texts (mutun) or is the saying of the Imam (Abu Hanifa), or is the apparent transmitted (zahir al-marwi), or is the major scholars' (jull al-izam).
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents a secondary rasm rule: if both conflicting opinions have been explicitly corrected (meaning each is considered valid within the madhhab), then in principle the mufti has discretion to choose either. However, this discretion is restricted by several weighting factors that tip the balance. Exceptions occur when: (1) one opinion is marked 'sahih' and the other 'asahh' – the stronger term indicates preference; (2) one is explicitly phrased as 'bihi yufata' (by it fatwa is given) – that one gains preponderance; (3) the opinion appears in the primary texts (mutun) of the madhhab, such as the works of al-Quduri or al-Hidayah; (4) it is the direct saying of Imam Abu Hanifa; (5) it is the apparent transmitted ruling (zahir al-riwaya); or (6) it is the view of the greatest scholars (jull al-izam). In any of these cases, the specified opinion becomes the mu'tamad and must be followed, removing the mufti's freedom to choose. The rule underscores that while tashih gives basic validity, additional markers of authority are necessary for final preference.

Key Terms
المتون (al-mutun): The authoritative primary texts of the Hanafi madhhab (e.g., Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Hidayah).
قول الإمام (qawl al-Imam): The direct saying of Imam Abu Hanifa himself.
ظاهر المروي (zahir al-marwi): The apparent or well-known transmitted ruling (from the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah).
جل العظام (jull al-'izam): The majority of the great scholars (e.g., Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and later authorities).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following does NOT give preponderance to one corrected opinion over another?
A) The opinion is in the mutun
B) The opinion is attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa
C) The opinion is explicitly stated as 'al-fatwa 'alayh'
D) The opinion is found in a later fatwa collection

Key Takeaway
When both opinions are corrected, the mufti's freedom is restricted by six authority markers that determine the mufta bihi.

Identifying the Mu'tamad Qawl Using Tasheeh Terms
Listing tasheeh terms and their relative strength for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the relative strength of tasheeh terms and apply the hierarchy to determine the mu'tamad qawl for fatwa.

Core Idea
The mufti must follow the strongest tasheeh term: 'alayhi al-fatwa' over 'sahih' or 'asahh'.

When a mufti encounters conflicting qawls in a mas'alah, later scholars often 'correct' (tasheeh) one of them using specific terms. This passage lists those terms in order of increasing strength, from 'al-fatwa alayh' to 'bihi yufta'. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for issuing reliable fatwas.

Guided Path
1
List all tasheeh terms
Read the passage and extract every term that indicates tasheeh. These include: 'al-fatwa alayh', 'al-ashbah', 'al-azhar', 'al-mukhtar', 'al-awjah', 'sahih', 'asahh', 'bihi yufta', and 'alayhi al-fatwa'.
2
Categorize by strength
Group the terms into two categories: the weaker group (the first five) and the stronger group ('sahih'/'asahh', and the strongest pair 'bihi yufta'/'alayhi al-fatwa'). Note that 'sahih' and 'asahh' have a minor dispute.
3
Analyze the sahih/asahh ikhtilaf
The author mentions that some hold 'asahh' as more emphatic, while others hold 'sahih' as more emphatic. Recognize this as a legitimate ikhtilaf among the muharrirun.
4
Identify the highest authority terms
According to the passage, 'bihi yufta' and 'alayhi al-fatwa' are stronger than all preceding terms. These are the most authoritative indicators that a qawl is mu'tamad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْفَتْوَى عَلَيْهِ، الْأَشْبَهُ، الْأظْهَر، الْمُخْتَارُ ذَا، والأوجه جیسے الفاظ سے، یاصحیح اور اصح کے الفاظ سے اور اصح کا لفظ صحیح سے زیادہ مؤکد ہے، اور ایک قول یہ ہے کہ صحیح کا لفظ اصح سے زیادہ مؤکد ہے، اسی طرح تصحیح کی گئی ہو بہ یفتی، یا علیه الفتوی سے اور یہ دونوں الفاظ سابقہ تمام الفاظ سے زیادہ قوت والے ہیں۔
The fatwa is upon it, the more similar, the more apparent, the chosen, the most appropriate, and such phrases, or with the words 'sahih' and 'asahh', and the word 'asahh' is more emphatic than 'sahih'. And one opinion is that the word 'sahih' is more emphatic than 'asahh'. Similarly, it is corrected with 'bihi yufta' or 'alayhi al-fatwa', and these two phrases are stronger than all the previous phrases.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage explains the rules for identifying the mu'tamad (relied-upon) qawl when a mufti finds that only one of two conflicting qawls has been explicitly corrected (tasheeh) by later scholars. The author lists the terms used to indicate tasheeh, in order of increasing strength: 'al-fatwa alayh', 'al-ashbah', 'al-azhar', 'al-mukhtar', 'al-awjah', then 'sahih' and 'asahh'. There is a disagreement among scholars about whether 'sahih' or 'asahh' is stronger; the author notes both views. The strongest indicators are 'bihi yufta' and 'alayhi al-fatwa', which explicitly state that the fatwa is based on that qawl. When any of these terms appear, the mufti must adopt that qawl without further deliberation.

Key Terms
الْفَتْوَى عَلَيْهِ (al-fatwa alayh): A phrase indicating that the mu'tamad position for issuing fatwa is this qawl
صحيح (sahih): A term denoting that this qawl is considered correct by the muharrir (editor)
أصح (asahh): A comparative term meaning 'more correct' than other qawls
به يفتى (bihi yufta): A phrase meaning 'by it a fatwa is given', indicating the mu'tamad position

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which phrase is considered the strongest indicator that a specific qawl is mu'tamad for fatwa?
A) الأشبه
B) المختار
C) عليه الفتوى
D) صحيح

Key Takeaway
The mufti must rely on the strongest tasheeh term; 'alayhi al-fatwa' and 'bihi yufta' are the most authoritative indicators.

Preferring Between Two Corrected Qawls in Hanafi Fatwa
Listing criteria for tarjih when two qawls are both corrected

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ten tarjih factors that break the tie between two corrected qawls and apply them to determine the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Two corrected qawls are equal unless one has a tarjih factor — then that qawl becomes the preferred opinion for fatwa.

When a mufti encounters two qawls that have both been explicitly corrected (mutamad), the default is that either may be chosen. However, the Hanafi school has enumerated specific factors that give one qawl preponderance (tarjih). This lesson unpacks those factors from the matn, guiding you through the hierarchy that a mufti must apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
The verse begins by stating that if you find two corrected qawls, you may choose either — each is reliable. This establishes the default: both are equally mu'tamad.
Default: free choice.
2
Recognize the exception clause
The verse then says 'إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَا صَحِيحاً وأصَحُ' — 'except when one is sahih and the other asahh'. This signals that certain factors override the default.
The word 'إِلَّا' introduces the exceptions.
3
List the ten tarjih factors
From the verse, extract each factor: (1) asahh vs sahih, (2) explicitly said to be fatwa basis, (3) found in mutun, (4) qawl of Imam, (5) from Zahir al-Riwayah, (6) held by majority of great jurists, (7) based on istihsan, (8) brings benefit to awqaf, (9) more suitable for the times, (10) clearer in evidence.
Memorize these factors as they are the core of the rule.
4
Understand the hierarchy
The factors are not ranked equally; some (like Zahir al-Riwayah or Imam's qawl) carry more weight. The mufti must weigh them if multiple factors are present.
In practice, the factor of being in the mutun or from Zahir al-Riwayah is often decisive.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given two corrected qawls on a case, check if any factor applies. If one qawl is from Zahir al-Riwayah and the other is not, the mufti must adopt the former.
This step operationalizes the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ تَجِدْ تَصْحِيْحَ قَوْلَيْنِ وَرَدْ فَاخْتَرُ لِمَا شِئْتَ، فَكُلُّ مُعْتَمَدْ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَا صَحِيحاً وأصَحُ أوُقِيلَ: ذَا يُفْتَى بِهِ فَقَدْ رَجَح أوْ كَانَ فِى المُتونِ أوْ قَوْلَ الْإِمَامُ أوْ ظَاهِرَ الْمَرُوِى أوُجُلُّ الْعِظَامُ قَالَ بِهِ، أَوْ كَانَ الإِسْتِحْسَانَا أوْ زَادَ لِلاوقَافِ نَفْعاً بَانَا أوْ كانَ ذَا أَوْفَقَ لِلزَّمَانِ أوْ كانَ ذَا أَوْضَحَ فِي الْبُرْهَانِ
And if you find correction of two qawls that have been narrated, then choose whichever you wish, for each is reliable. Except when they are sahih and asahh, or it was said: 'this is used for fatwa' then it has preponderance; or if it is in the texts (mutun), or the saying of the Imam, or from Zahir al-Riwayah, or the great jurists (including the 'ulama) said it; or it is based on istihsan; or it brings clear benefit for awqaf; or it is more in harmony with the times; or it is clearer in evidence.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where a mufti finds two different qawls both explicitly corrected (mutamad). The general rule is that both are equally valid, so the mufti may choose either. However, there are exceptions (mustathniyat) where one qawl becomes preferable. These tarjih factors are: (1) If one uses the comparative term 'asahh' and the other 'sahih' (since 'asahh' is stronger per dominant view); (2) If one qawl is explicitly said to be the basis of fatwa; (3) If one qawl is found in the mutun (core texts); (4) If one qawl is directly from Imam Abu Hanifa; (5) If one qawl is from Zahir al-Riwayah; (6) If one qawl is held by the majority of great jurists; (7) If one qawl is based on istihsan; (8) If one qawl brings clear benefit to awqaf; (9) If one qawl is more suitable for the current time; (10) If one qawl has stronger evidentiary proof. In any of these cases, the mufti must adopt the qawl with the tarjih factor.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six books
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that departs from strict analogy for a more equitable result

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a tarjih factor mentioned for preferring one corrected qawl over another?
A) Being in the mutun
B) Being qawl of Imam Abu Hanifa
C) Being based on qiyas jaliy
D) Being from Zahir al-Riwayah

Key Takeaway
When two corrected qawls conflict, the mufti may choose either unless one qawl has a specific tarjih factor from the list — then that qawl becomes the mu'tamad.

The Ten Preference Factors for Tarjih
Lists the ten murajjihaat for resolving ta'arud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ten preference factors for tarjih when two authentic sayings conflict, and apply them to identify the mufta bihi in a given case.

Core Idea
When two sayings are both authentic, the mufti must use ten objective criteria – not whim – to choose.

A mufti often encounters two equally authentic narrations on the same issue. This passage from Naseem al-Mufti lays out the ten factors that settle such conflicts. These criteria are part of the mufti's toolkit (rasm al-mufti) and ensure that the operative ruling is chosen on sound methodological grounds, not personal preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict
Determine that two sayings are both authentically narrated (sahih or asahh) and that they contradict each other. If not, tarjih rules do not apply.
2
Check for explicit fatwa statement
If one saying is explicitly marked 'upon it is the fatwa', that saying is automatically preferred.
This overrides other factors.
3
Scan the ten factors
Go through each of the ten murajjihaat: being asahh vs sahih, in the matn, saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, from Zahir al-Riwayah, followed by many jurists, based on istihsan, beneficial for awqaf, suitable for the time, clearer in proof, or majority of great scholars hold it.
Any single factor is sufficient.
4
Apply the factor
Select the saying that possesses any of these factors. If both have factors, the one with the higher number of factors or the more authoritative factor according to hierarchy is chosen.
The passage does not rank them explicitly, but later Hanafi works give some ordering.
5
Issue the fatwa
The chosen saying becomes the mufta bihi (operative position) for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسيم المفتى في جل صاحت
(۳۹)
شن عقود رسم المفتى
قَالَ بِهِ، أَوْ كَانَ الإِسْتِحْسَانَا ٦٤ أو زَادَ لِلاوقَافِ نَفْعاً بَانَا أوْ كانَ ذَا أَوْفَقَ لِلزَّمَانِ ۲۵ أوْ كانَ ذَا أَوْضَحَ فِي الْبُرْهَانِ ترجمہ: اور اگر آپ تصحیح پائیں دو ایسے اقوال کی جن میں سے ہر ایک قول مروی ہو تو آپ ان میں سے جس کا چاہیں انتخاب کرلیں ، اس لیے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک قول قابل اعتماد ہے، مگر جب دونوں صحیح واصبح ہوں (یعنی ایک قول میں صحیح کا لفظ ہو اور دوسرے قول میں اصح کا لفظ ہو ) ، یا کسی ایک کے بارے میں ) کہا گیا ہو کہ اس قول پر فتوی ہے تو یقیناً وہی قول راجح ہوگا ، یا ان میں سے ایک قول متون میں ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول امام اعظم کا ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول ظاہر الروایہ میں ہو ، یا ان میں سے ایک قول کے قائل بڑے بڑے فقہاء ہوں، یا ان میں سے ایک قول استحسان پر مبنی ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول اوقاف کے لیے واضح طور پر نفع بخش ہو یا ان میں سے ایک قول زمانہ سے زیادہ ہم آہنگ ہو، یا ان میں سے ایک قول دلیل میں واضح تر ہو ( تو ان تمام صورتوں میں جس قول میں مذکورہ بالا وجوہ ترجیح میں سے کوئی وجہ ترجیح مل جائے اسی قول پر فتوی دیں گے)۔ دو قول کی کہیں پر صحیح آپ دیکھیں

سم المفتى فى حل مباد مباحث
یا ایک قول ان میں ہو ظاہر الروایہ یا پھر بڑوں نے ہم کو وہ قول ہو بتایا
شن عقود رسم المفى ا
یا قول وہ جو ٹھہرے استحسان کا نتیجہ یا وقف کے لئے ہو وہ قول فائدے کا
یا قول وہ زمانہ کے حسب حال ٹھہرے
یا قول وہ درایت میں سب سے بڑھ کے نکلے
هَذَا إِذَا تَعَارَضَ التَّصْحِيحُ ٢٦ أَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ أَصْلاً بِهِ تَصْرِيحُ فَتَأْخُذُ الَّذِى لَهُ مُرَبِّحُ ٦٧ مِمَّا عَلِمْتَهُ، فَهَذَا الْأَوْضَحُ ترجمہ: یہ ترجیح والی بات اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ دو اقوال کی تصحیح میں تعارض ہو جائے یا شیح کی بالکل صراحت نہ ہو، پس اس قول پر عمل کرو جس قول میں ان مرجحات میں سے کوئی وجہ ترجیح ہو جن کو آپ جان چکے ہیں، پس یہ نہایت واضح بات ہے۔ یہ جب ہے جب تعارض تصحیح میں کہیں
ہو
یا جب ہے جب کہ کوئی تصریح ہی نہیں ہو
اب آپ قول وہ لیں ترجیح جس کی دیکھیں
کل دس وجوہ ترجیح یہ تھیں جو پڑھ چکے ہیں
He said, or it was istihsan, or it increased benefit for endowments, or it was more suitable for the time, or it was clearer in proof. Translation: And if you find authentication of two sayings, each of which is narrated, you may choose whichever you wish, because each is reliable. However, when both are sahih and asahh (i.e., one is said to be sahih and the other asahh), or it was said about one that the fatwa is upon it, then undoubtedly that saying is preponderant. Or one of them is in the matn, or one is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, or one is in Zahir al-Riwayah, or one is followed by great jurists, or one is based on istihsan, or one is clearly beneficial for endowments, or one is more in harmony with the time, or one is clearer in evidence. This is when there is conflict in authentication, or there is no explicit statement at all. So take the saying that has a preferencing factor from what you have learned; this is the clearest.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents the rules of tarjih (preference) for a mufti when two conflicting sayings are both authentically narrated. The author lists ten preference factors: (1) being called 'asahh' (more correct) over 'sahih', (2) explicit statement that fatwa is upon it, (3) inclusion in the matn (core texts), (4) being the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, (5) being from Zahir al-Riwayah, (6) followed by majority of jurists, (7) based on istihsan, (8) beneficial for awqaf, (9) more suitable for the time, (10) clearer in proof. The rule applies when there is genuine ta'arud (conflict) in authentication or when no explicit preference is stated. The mufti then selects the saying with any of these preferencing factors.

Key Terms
تصحیح (tas'hih): The process of authenticating or declaring a saying as sound (sahih) in the madhhab.
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict between two equally authentic sayings regarding the same issue.
مرجحات (murajjihaat): Factors that give preponderance to one saying over another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Choose arbitrarily
B) Apply the ten preference factors
C) Refer to the earliest source
D) Follow the majority of later scholars

Key Takeaway
When two authentic sayings conflict, the mufti must apply the ten objective factors (murajjihaat) to determine the preponderant position.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
