In this regard, there is disagreement among the scholars: The first saying is that in any case, they will give fatwa on the saying of Imam A'zam and will not depart from it. This is the saying of Hadhrat Abdullah ibn Mubarak. The second saying is that the mufti will have absolute choice; if he wishes, he may give fatwa on the saying of Imam A'zam...
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This seventh principle deals with the unresolved scenario: when Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on a matter that is not related to changing custom. Here, later scholars themselves disagreed. One position (from Abdullah ibn Mubarak) insists on always following Imam Abu Hanifa. The other position gives the mufti full discretion to choose either opinion. The text is cut off, so we do not have the full second view or any preferred tarjih. This shows that even within the Hanafi tradition, some methodological questions remained open. A mufti in such a case would need to be aware of this ikhtilaf and may follow the majority practice or the stronger view from other authorities.

Key Terms
عبد اللہ بن مبارک (Abdullah ibn Mubarak): A prominent early Hanafi scholar (d. 181 AH) known for his piety and jurisprudence; his view is cited as the first opinion in this dispute.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf (d. 182 AH) and Muhammad al-Shaybani (d. 189 AH). They are the primary transmitters and developers of Hanafi fiqh.
رسل المفتي (Rasm al-Mufti): The rules and methodology that a mufti must follow when issuing fatwas, including principles for preferring one opinion over another.

Fifth Principle: Preference of Imam A'zam's View
Rule for mufti when Hanafi imams differ without preponderance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fifth principle of Rasm al-Mufti to identify the operative opinion (mufta bihi) when the three Hanafi imams differ and no preponderance has been established by the people of tarjih.

Core Idea
When the three imams differ without a preferred view, the mufti must adopt Imam A'zam's opinion.

This lesson introduces a foundational rule for muftis when navigating ikhtilaf among the founding Hanafi imams. The fifth principle of Rasm al-Mufti provides a clear default: if no later scholar has given preponderance to any opinion, the mufti must follow Imam Abu Hanifa. This ensures consistency and authority in fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the condition
Recognize that the principle applies when all three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) have separate sayings on the same issue, and the later scholars (ashab al-tarjih) have not declared any opinion as preponderant.
This condition is crucial: if any opinion has been preponderated, that opinion takes precedence.
2
State the default ruling
The mufti must (lazim) give fatwa according to Imam A'zam's opinion. This is the operative ruling unless a severe necessity (darura shadida) exists.
Severe necessity is a high bar—e.g., widespread hardship or inability to practice the default.
3
Note the reinforcement clause
If one of the two companions (Abu Yusuf or Muhammad) agrees with Imam Abu Hanifa, then there is no doubt; the majority (or at least two of the three) strengthens the preponderance.
This clause removes ambiguity: no need for further tarjih.
4
Identify the exception
Deviation from Imam A'zam's opinion is not permissible except under severe necessity. The mufti must justify such deviation.
The concept of darura is defined elsewhere in usul al-fiqh; it is not arbitrary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پانچواں اصول : جب کسی مسئلہ میں احناف کا اختلاف ہو ۔ شن عقود رسم المفى ا‌ ‌جب کسی مسئلہ میں احناف کے ائمہ ثلاثہ یعنی امام ابوحنیفہ، امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد میں سے ہر ایک سے مختلف اقوال مروی ہوں، بایں طور کہ ہر ایک کا الگ الگ قول ہو اور اصحاب الترجیح نے کسی قول کو راجح ن قرار دیا ہو تو امام اعظم کے قول پر فتوی دینا لازم ہوگا اور بغیر کسی شدید ضرورت کے ان کے قول سے عدول کرنا جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ نیز امام صاحب کا قول اس صورت میں بھی راج ہو گا جب کہ صاحبین میں سے کسی ایک کا قول امام اعظم کے قول کے موافق ہو۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی : ۱۰۲ ، فتاوی قاضی خان (۹/۱)
Fifth principle: When there is disagreement among the Hanafis. In the commentary of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: When different sayings are reported from each of the three Hanafi imams, i.e., Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad, such that each has a separate saying and the people of tarjih have not declared any saying as preponderant, then giving fatwa according to the saying of Imam A'zam is necessary, and it is not permissible to deviate from his saying without any severe necessity. Also, the saying of Imam Sahib is preponderant even when one of the two companions (Sahibayn) agrees with the saying of Imam A'zam. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 102, Fatawa Qadi Khan 9/1)
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth principle for a mufti when the three main Hanafi imams have differing opinions on a matter and no later scholar has given preponderance to one view. The rule is clear: the mufti must follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion as the default, and it is impermissible to depart from it except under dire necessity. Furthermore, if either Abu Yusuf or Muhammad al-Shaybani agrees with Abu Hanifa, that reinforces the preponderance—so there is no doubt. This principle reflects the high authority of the founding imam in the Hanafi school, particularly when his own students do not produce a collectively preponderant view.

Key Terms
ائمہ ثلاثہ (a'imma thalatha): The three main Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
اصحاب الترجیح (ashab al-tarjih): Scholars who have the authority to determine which opinion is preponderant (rajih) based on evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When there is severe necessity (darura shadida)
C) When the majority of later scholars favor another view
D) Never, under any circumstances

Key Takeaway
When the three Hanafi imams differ and no later preponderance exists, the mufti's default is Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, deviation only under severe necessity.

Sixth Principle: Custom-Based Differences
Rasm al-mufti rule: preferring Sahibayn when custom changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the sixth principle of rasm al-mufti to identify when the Sahibayn's view is preponderant over Imam Abu Hanifa's due to a change in custom.

Core Idea
When custom changes, the later fatwa of the Sahibayn overrides Imam Abu Hanifa's earlier ruling.

In Hanafi ifta methodology, not every difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his students is equal. Some disputes arise from shifts in social conditions and customs ('urf). This principle, known as the sixth principle of rasm al-mufti, guides the mufti: if the basis of the disagreement is a change in custom, the later opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani becomes the operative position. We'll explore how to diagnose such differences and apply the rule correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize when Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ on a ruling. The difference could be in any chapter of fiqh.
2
Diagnose the cause
Determine whether the disagreement is rooted in a change of custom or time (as opposed to a purely textual or methodological difference). Look for evidence in the reasoning: did Imam Abu Hanifa cite a specific practice of his era, and did the Sahibayn mention a changed practice?
If the cause is not custom, the rule does not apply automatically.
3
Apply the maxim
If the difference is indeed based on a shift in custom, the later view of the Sahibayn becomes preponderant (raajih). The governing maxim is 'al-‘ādatu muḥakkamah' (custom is authoritative). The mufti must adopt the Sahibayn's ruling.
The maxim is a major legal principle (qa'ida kubra) in the Hanafi school.
4
Verify the custom's validity
Ensure the later custom is widespread, consistent, and not opposed to any explicit Shari'ah text. If the custom is isolated or sinful, the principle does not apply.
This verification is crucial; not every change qualifies.
5
Issue the fatwa
Deliver the fatwa based on the Sahibayn's view, with proper attribution. Document that the change in custom necessitated the shift.
The mufta bihi is the later, custom-based opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چھٹا اصول: امام اعظم اور صاحبین کا اختلاف عصر و زمان پر مبنی ہو ا ‌جب کسی مسئلہ میں امام ابوحنیفہ ایک جانب ہوں اور دوسری جانب ان کے اصحاب یا صاحبین ہوں تو اگر ان کے اختلاف کا دارو مدار عصر و زمان پر ہو، بایں طور کہ امام صاحب نے اپنے زمانہ کے احوال اور عرف کے مطابق فتوی دیا ہو اور اصحاب کے زمانہ میں عرف اور احوال میں تبدیلی ہونے کی وجہ سے اصحاب نے دوسرے قول پر فتوی دیا ہو تو اس صورت میں صاحبین اور دیگر اصحاب کا قول ہی راجح ہوگا، کیوں کہ عرف کی تبدیلی سے احکام میں تبدیلی ہوتی رہتی ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی:۱۰۳،فتاوی قاضی خان: ۹/۱)
Sixth principle: The difference between Imam A'zam and the two companions (Sahibayn) is based on era and time. When in a matter Imam Abu Hanifa is on one side and on the other side are his students or the two companions, and if the basis of their difference is era and time, such that Imam Sahib gave a fatwa according to the conditions and custom of his time, and due to change in custom and conditions in the time of the students, they gave fatwa on another saying, then in this case the saying of the Sahibayn and other students is preponderant, because with the change of custom, rulings keep changing. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 103, Fatawa Qadi Khan: 9/1)
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This is the sixth principle addressing differences that stem from changing social conditions and customs. Imam Abu Hanifa might have ruled based on the 'urf (custom) of his era, but if that custom changed by the time of his students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, then their later ruling becomes preponderant. The operative cause is the change in 'urf, a well-established Hanafi maxim: 'al-‘ādatu muḥakkamah' (custom is authoritative). The mufti must assess whether the difference is driven by time and place; if so, the later view of the Sahibayn carries more weight.

Key Terms
عرف (urf): Custom or common practice that is not opposed to Shari'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Sahibayn are more knowledgeable
B) The difference is based on a change in custom and time
C) The Sahibayn's view is easier
D) A later consensus preferred them

Key Takeaway
When a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn is caused by a change in custom, the Sahibayn's later opinion becomes the muftā bihi.

Three Views on Choosing Between Imam A'zam and Sahibayn
Presents three scholarly views and their reconciliation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scholarly views on whether to follow Imam A'zam or the Sahibayn when their difference is not custom-based, and explain how the third view reconciles the first two.

Core Idea
When Imam A'zam and his students differ, the mufti's level of ijtihad determines which view to follow.

This lesson examines a key principle in Hanafi fatwa methodology: how to choose between the opinions of Imam A'zam and his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, when their difference is not rooted in changing customs. Three distinct positions have been recorded among early scholars. Understanding them is essential for any mufti or student of fiqh to correctly navigate the school's hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
The issue arises when Imam Abu Hanifa holds one position and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold another, and the disagreement is not due to changes in custom or time. The question is: which opinion should a mufti follow?
This is distinct from differences based on custom (urf), which are addressed in earlier principles.
2
State the First View
Abdullah ibn Mubarak held that the mufti must always follow Imam A'zam's opinion without exception. This view gives absolute priority to the founder of the school.
This reflects a strict adherence to the founding imam's authority.
3
State the Second View
Some early scholars gave the mufti absolute freedom to choose between Imam A'zam's opinion and that of the Sahibayn, based on what he deemed most appropriate.
This grants wide discretion, but may lead to inconsistency.
4
State the Third View (Reconciliation)
The third view distinguishes between a mujtahid mufti (one qualified to weigh evidence) and a non-mujtahid (muqallid) mufti. A mujtahid may choose based on evidence; a non-mujtahid is bound to follow Imam A'zam.
This view reconciles the first two by assigning each to a different category of mufti.
5
Understand the Reconciliation
The author notes that the third view harmonizes the earlier positions: Abdullah ibn Mubarak's view applies to non-mujtahid muftis, while the second view applies to mujtahid muftis. There is no real contradiction.
This is consistent with Hanafi usul, where ijtihad capacity dictates the scope of choice.

ساتواں اصول: امام اعظم اور صاحبین کا اختلاف عصر و زمان پرمنی نہ ہو ‌جب کسی مسئلہ میں امام ابو حنیفہ ایک جانب ہوں اور دوسری جانب ان کے اصحاب یا صاحبین ہوں اور ان کے اختلاف کا دارو مدار عصر و زمان پر نہ ہو تو کن کے قول پر فتوی دیں گے اس سلسلہ میں علماء کے درمیان اختلاف ہے: پہلا قول یہ ہے کہ بہر صورت امام اعظم کے قول پر فتوی دیں گے اور اس سے عدول نہیں کریں گے، یہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن مبارک کا قول ہے، دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ مفتی کو مطلقا اختیار ہوگا ، اگر چاہے تو امام اعظم کے قول پر فتوی دے اور اگر چاہے تو صاحبین کے قول پر فتوی دے، تیسرا قول یہ ہے کہ مفتی اگر مجتہد ہو تو سے اختیار ہو گا، وہ دلیل کے اعتبار سے جس قول کو راج سمجھے اسی پر فتوی دے اور اگر مفتی غیر مجتہد ہو تو وہ امام اعظم کے قول پر فتوی دینے کا پابند ہوگا۔ واضح ہو کہ یہ تیسرا اقول دراصل کا پہلے اور دوسرے قول میں تطبیق کی ایک شکل ہے کہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن مبارک کا قول مفتی غیر مجتہد سے متعلق ہے اور دوسرا قول مجتہد مفتی کے ساتھ خاص ہے، پس اس اعتبار سے دونوں اقوال میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہوگا، کیوں کہ دونوں کا مصداق الگ الگ ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ۱۰۲ ،فتاوی قاضی خان: ۹/۱ ، الحاوى القدسي : ٥٦٢/٢)
فائدہ: علامہ شامی فرماتے ہیں کہ ہمارے زمانہ میں مجتہد مفتی کا پایا جانا مشکل ہے اور غیر مجتہد مفتی میں دلیل کے اعتبار سے کسی قول کو ترجیح دینے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہے، لہذا اب بہر صورت امام اعظم کا قول راج ہوگا، مگر یہ کہ اصحاب الترجیح کسی دوسرے قول کو راجح قرار دیں۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ١٠٦)
Seventh principle: The difference between Imam A'zam and the two companions (Sahibayn) is not based on era and time. When in a matter Imam Abu Hanifa is on one side and on the other side are his students or the two companions, and the basis of their difference is not era and time, then on whose saying will fatwa be given? There is difference among scholars: The first saying is that in any case fatwa will be given according to the saying of Imam A'zam and they will not deviate from it; this is the saying of Hadrat Abdullah ibn Mubarak. The second saying is that the mufti has absolute choice; if he wishes, he may give fatwa on Imam A'zam's saying, and if he wishes, on the saying of the Sahibayn. The third saying is that if the mufti is a mujtahid, then he has choice; he will give fatwa on whichever saying he considers preponderant based on evidence; and if the mufti is not a mujtahid, then he is bound to give fatwa on Imam A'zam's saying. It is clear that this third saying is actually a reconciliation of the first and second sayings: the saying of Hadrat Abdullah ibn Mubarak pertains to a non-mujtahid mufti, and the second saying is specific to a mujtahid mufti. Thus from this perspective there is no contradiction between the two sayings, because the referent of each is different. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 102, Fatawa Qadi Khan: 9/1, al-Hawi al-Qudsi: 2/562)
Benefit: Allamah Shami says that in our time, finding a mujtahid mufti is difficult, and a non-mujtahid mufti does not have the ability to prefer one saying over another based on evidence. Therefore now in any case the saying of Imam A'zam is preponderant, unless the people of tarjih declare another saying as preponderant. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 106)
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh principle dealing with differences that are not rooted in changing custom. Three distinct positions are recorded: (1) Abdullah ibn Mubarak insisted on always following Imam A'zam, (2) some gave the mufti complete freedom, (3) a reconciling view distinguishes between mujtahid and non-mujtahid muftis. The author favors the third view as harmonizing the first two. Then a crucial practical note (fā'idah) from Allamah Shami (Ibn 'Abidin) states that in later times, mujtahids are virtually nonexistent, so non-mujtahid muftis are bound to follow Imam A'zam unless later scholars (ashab al-tarjih) have explicitly preponderated another view. This reflects the gradual crystallization of the Hanafi school and the reduction of ijtihad.

Key Terms
مجتہد مفتی (mujtahid mufti): A mufti who possesses the ability to derive rulings from evidence and weigh conflicting opinions by ijtihad.
فقیر غیر مجتہد (ghayr mujtahid): A mufti who lacks the capacity for independent reasoning and is bound to follow the school's established rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciling third view, who is allowed to choose between Imam A'zam and the Sahibayn in non-custom differences?
A) Any mufti regardless of qualification
B) Only mujtahid muftis
C) Only non-mujtahid muftis
D) Only the scholar Abdullah ibn Mubarak

Key Takeaway
When Imam A'zam and the Sahibayn differ on non-custom matters, non-mujtahid muftis must follow Imam A'zam, while mujtahid muftis may choose based on evidence.
